The Proof of Universal Prophethood and Finality
Proof of Muhammad's universal mission and finality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an and miracles prove that Muhammad's prophethood is universal and final.

Core Idea
Muhammad's prophethood is for all, proven by his claim, miracle, and the Qur'an's testimony.

In this section, the author refutes the claim that only Arabs needed a prophet and provides the core evidence for Muhammad's universal mission and his status as the seal of the prophets. The passage establishes that his claim was explicit and supported by his miraculous book, the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the translation. Notice how the author refutes the claim that only Arabs needed a prophet.
The passage builds on the earlier discussion of the need for a renewer of the law.
2
Identify the three components of the proof
The author gives three reasons for universality: Muhammad's explicit claim, the miracle he manifested, and the Qur'an's testimony. Find each in the text.
The Qur'anic verses cited are key evidence.
3
Reflect on the significance of finality
Consider why the author links universality with finality. How does the claim of being the 'seal of the prophets' reinforce the universal scope?
No prophet after him means his message is the final and universal one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يريد أنه مبعوث إلى الثقلين، لا إلى العرب خاصة، على ما زعم بعض اليهود والنصارى زعماً منهم أن الاحتياج إلى النبي إنما كان للعرب خاصة دون أهل الكتابين ورد بما مر من احتياج الكل إلى من يجدد أمر الشريعة، بل احتياج اليهود والنصارى أكثر لاختلال دينهم بالتجريفات وأنواع الضلالات، مع ادعائهم أنه من عند الله تعالى والدليل على عموم بعثته وكونه خاتم النبيين، لا نبي بعده، ولا نسخ لشريعته هو أنه ادعى ذلك بحيث لا يحتمل التأويل، وأظهر المعجزة على وفقه وأن كتابه المعجز قد شهد بذلك قطعاً كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَاكَ إِلَّا كَافَّةً لِلنَّاسِ﴾ ﴿قُلْ إِنِّي رَسُولُ اللهِ إِلَيْكُمْ جَمِيعًا﴾ ﴿قُلْ أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ أَنَّهُ اسْتَمَعَ نَفَرٌ مِنَ الْجِنِّ﴾ الآيات و﴿لَكِنْ رَسُولَ اللهِ وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّينَ﴾ ﴿لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ﴾ . لا يقال : ففي القرآن ما يدل على أن التوراة والإنجيل هدى للناس من غير تفرقة بين ما يوافق القرآن ويخالفه، فيختص هداية القرآن وبعثة محمد (عليه السلام) بقومه الذين هم العرب على ما يشير إليه بقوله : ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِنْ رَسُولٍ إِلَّا بِلِسَانِ قَوْمِهِ﴾ . لأنا نقول : هما هدى للناس من قبل نزول القرآن أو هدى لهم إلى الإيمان .
He means that he (Muhammad) was sent to the two weighty ones (humans and jinn), not to the Arabs specifically, contrary to the claim of some Jews and Christians who allege that the need for a prophet was only for the Arabs, not for the People of the Book. This is refuted by what has already been mentioned regarding the need of all for one who renews the matter of the law; indeed the need of the Jews and Christians is greater due to the corruption of their religion through alterations and various errors, despite their claim that it is from God Almighty. And the proof of the universality of his mission and that he is the seal of the prophets, no prophet after him, and no abrogation of his law, is that he claimed that in a manner not subject to interpretation, and he manifested a miracle in accordance with it, and his miraculous book testifies to it definitively, such as His saying: 'And We have not sent you except as a bringer of good tidings to all mankind' and 'Say, I am the messenger of God to you all' and 'Say, It has been revealed to me that a group of jinn listened' and the verses, and 'But the messenger of God and the seal of the prophets' and 'to make it prevail over all religion'. It cannot be said: In the Qur'an there is evidence that the Torah and the Gospel are guidance for people without distinction between what agrees with the Qur'an and what contradicts it, so the guidance of the Qur'an and the mission of Muhammad (peace be upon him) are specific to his people who are the Arabs, as indicated by His saying: 'And We did not send any messenger except in the language of his people'. For we say: Those two (Torah and Gospel) were guidance for people before the revelation of the Qur'an, or they were guidance for them to faith.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the previous section and contains a proof and an objection-and-answer. The author explains that the intended meaning of the earlier statements is that Muhammad was sent to all of humanity and jinn, not only to Arabs, contrary to a claim attributed to some Jews and Christians that only Arabs needed a prophet because they were unlettered, while the People of the Book had scriptures. The author refutes this by reiterating the general need for a renewer of the law, emphasizing that Jews and Christians were in greater need due to corruption in their religions. Then the author provides the proof for Muhammad's universal mission and finality: Muhammad explicitly claimed such, his miracle (the Qur'an) confirmed his claim, and the Qur'an itself testifies definitively with verses like 34:28, 7:158, 72:1-4, 33:40, and 9:33. A potential objection is then raised: does not the Qur'an say that the Torah and Gospel were guidance for all people, and that every messenger was sent in the language of his people, implying that the Qur'an and Muhammad's mission are only for Arabs? The author answers that the Torah and Gospel were guidance before the Qur'an was revealed, or they were guidance specifically for attaining faith (not for all legal rulings). Thus, the universality of Muhammad's mission remains intact.

Key Terms
الثقلين
خاتم النبيين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the author prove Muhammad's universal prophethood?
A) By citing only one verse
B) By three evidences: explicit claim, miracle, and Qur'anic testimony
C) By saying that Jews and Christians needed it more
D) By logical deduction without scripture

Key Takeaway
Muhammad's universal prophethood and finality are proven by his explicit claim, the miracle of the Qur'an, and the Qur'an's own testimony.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author argues that the need for a prophet is greater for those whose scriptures are corrupted. How has your own understanding of Islam been corrupted by neglect or incorrect teachings? What specific step will you take this week to realign yourself with the authentic message of the Prophet?
?
The proof of Muhammad's finality includes that he performed a miracle—the Qur'an—to back his claim. Have you ever treated the Qur'an as a mere book of blessings rather than the decisive proof it is? How will you change your engagement with the Qur'an to make it the foundation of your certainty?
?
The Prophet was sent to both humans and jinn. Does your daily life reflect that you are accountable to an audience beyond the visible? What would change in your private actions if you truly believed the jinn are watching and learning from your example?

Responding to the Language Objection
Objection and answer about the language of revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how to resolve the apparent conflict between the verse 'We sent no messenger except in the language of his people' and Muhammad's universal mission.

Core Idea
The language of revelation does not limit the scope of prophethood.

A potential objection arises from the Qur'anic verse that every messenger was sent in the language of his own people, which some might use to argue that Muhammad's mission was only for Arabs. The author provides a clear answer that preserves the universality of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic objection starting with 'لا يقال' and the answer 'لأنا نقول'. Understand the logic of the objection and the two-pronged answer.
The objection relies on a seeming contradiction between universal verses and the language verse.
2
Analyze the two parts of the answer
The author gives two possible interpretations of the Torah and Gospel being 'guidance for people'. Identify both and see how they neutralize the objection.
The answer does not deny the verse but contextualizes it.
3
Connect back to the earlier proof
See how this answer supports the main thesis of universal prophethood. Why does this objection matter?
If left unanswered, it would undermine the proof just established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يريد أنه مبعوث إلى الثقلين، لا إلى العرب خاصة، على ما زعم بعض اليهود والنصارى زعماً منهم أن الاحتياج إلى النبي إنما كان للعرب خاصة دون أهل الكتابين ورد بما مر من احتياج الكل إلى من يجدد أمر الشريعة، بل احتياج اليهود والنصارى أكثر لاختلال دينهم بالتجريفات وأنواع الضلالات، مع ادعائهم أنه من عند الله تعالى والدليل على عموم بعثته وكونه خاتم النبيين، لا نبي بعده، ولا نسخ لشريعته هو أنه ادعى ذلك بحيث لا يحتمل التأويل، وأظهر المعجزة على وفقه وأن كتابه المعجز قد شهد بذلك قطعاً كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَاكَ إِلَّا كَافَّةً لِلنَّاسِ﴾ ﴿قُلْ إِنِّي رَسُولُ اللهِ إِلَيْكُمْ جَمِيعًا﴾ ﴿قُلْ أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ أَنَّهُ اسْتَمَعَ نَفَرٌ مِنَ الْجِنِّ﴾ الآيات و﴿لَكِنْ رَسُولَ اللهِ وَخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّينَ﴾ ﴿لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ﴾ . لا يقال : ففي القرآن ما يدل على أن التوراة والإنجيل هدى للناس من غير تفرقة بين ما يوافق القرآن ويخالفه، فيختص هداية القرآن وبعثة محمد (عليه السلام) بقومه الذين هم العرب على ما يشير إليه بقوله : ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِنْ رَسُولٍ إِلَّا بِلِسَانِ قَوْمِهِ﴾ . لأنا نقول : هما هدى للناس من قبل نزول القرآن أو هدى لهم إلى الإيمان .
He means that he (Muhammad) was sent to the two weighty ones (humans and jinn), not to the Arabs specifically, contrary to the claim of some Jews and Christians who allege that the need for a prophet was only for the Arabs, not for the People of the Book. This is refuted by what has already been mentioned regarding the need of all for one who renews the matter of the law; indeed the need of the Jews and Christians is greater due to the corruption of their religion through alterations and various errors, despite their claim that it is from God Almighty. And the proof of the universality of his mission and that he is the seal of the prophets, no prophet after him, and no abrogation of his law, is that he claimed that in a manner not subject to interpretation, and he manifested a miracle in accordance with it, and his miraculous book testifies to it definitively, such as His saying: 'And We have not sent you except as a bringer of good tidings to all mankind' and 'Say, I am the messenger of God to you all' and 'Say, It has been revealed to me that a group of jinn listened' and the verses, and 'But the messenger of God and the seal of the prophets' and 'to make it prevail over all religion'. It cannot be said: In the Qur'an there is evidence that the Torah and the Gospel are guidance for people without distinction between what agrees with the Qur'an and what contradicts it, so the guidance of the Qur'an and the mission of Muhammad (peace be upon him) are specific to his people who are the Arabs, as indicated by His saying: 'And We did not send any messenger except in the language of his people'. For we say: Those two (Torah and Gospel) were guidance for people before the revelation of the Qur'an, or they were guidance for them to faith.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the previous section and contains a proof and an objection-and-answer. The author explains that the intended meaning of the earlier statements is that Muhammad was sent to all of humanity and jinn, not only to Arabs, contrary to a claim attributed to some Jews and Christians that only Arabs needed a prophet because they were unlettered, while the People of the Book had scriptures. The author refutes this by reiterating the general need for a renewer of the law, emphasizing that Jews and Christians were in greater need due to corruption in their religions. Then the author provides the proof for Muhammad's universal mission and finality: Muhammad explicitly claimed such, his miracle (the Qur'an) confirmed his claim, and the Qur'an itself testifies definitively with verses like 34:28, 7:158, 72:1-4, 33:40, and 9:33. A potential objection is then raised: does not the Qur'an say that the Torah and Gospel were guidance for all people, and that every messenger was sent in the language of his people, implying that the Qur'an and Muhammad's mission are only for Arabs? The author answers that the Torah and Gospel were guidance before the Qur'an was revealed, or they were guidance specifically for attaining faith (not for all legal rulings). Thus, the universality of Muhammad's mission remains intact.

هدى

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the verse 'We sent no messenger except in the language of his people' limits Muhammad's prophethood to Arabs only.
Correction: The author explains that this verse refers to the medium of communication, not the geographical or ethnic scope. Muhammad's mission is universal despite the Qur'an being revealed in Arabic.

Key Takeaway
The objection based on the language verse is resolved by clarifying that the Torah and Gospel were either temporary guidance or faith guidance, not rival universal systems.

The Universal Mission and Seal of Prophethood
The author proves the universal mission of Prophet Muhammad and refutes objections about previous scriptures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational and scriptural basis for Prophet Muhammad's universal mission and his seal of prophethood, and how the author refutes objections based on previous scriptures.

Core Idea
Muhammad (saw) was sent to all, not just Arabs — the Quran and miracles prove it.

The author addresses a key doubt: if prior scriptures were for all, why a new prophet? He argues that all people, especially Jews and Christians, needed a renewer, and the Quran itself proclaims universality. Let's trace his argument step by step, from refuting a false claim to answering a subtle objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the objection-and-answer structure.
2
Identify the claim being refuted
Find where the author mentions what some Jews and Christians claimed. What is their argument about prophethood being only for Arabs?
3
Note the evidence for universality
The author presents evidence: the Prophet's clear claim, miracles, and Quranic verses. List the verses he quotes.
Observe that the verses are given as partial quotations.
4
Understand the objection from previous scriptures
The author anticipates: 'But the Torah and Gospel are called guidance for all people.' Why could this be seen as a problem for universal prophethood?
5
See the author's response
How does the author answer that objection? He gives two interpretations of those scriptures being 'guidance for people.' What are they?
This is the key to resolving the apparent conflict.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يريد أنه مبعوث إلى الثقلين، لا إلى العرب خاصة، على ما زعم بعض اليهود والنصارى زعماً منهم أن الاحتياج إلى النبي إنما كان للعرب خاصة دون أهل الكتابين ورد بما مر من احتياج الكل إلى من يجدد أمر الشريعة، بل احتياج اليهود والنصارى أكثر لاختلال دينهم بالتجريفات وأنواع الضلالات، مع ادعائهم أنه من عند الله تعالى والدليل على عموم بعثته وكونه خاتم النبيين، لا نبي بعده، ولا نسخ لشريعته هو أنه ادعى ذلك بحيث لا يحتمل التأويل، وأظهر المعجزة على وفقه وأن كتابه المعجز قد شهد بذلك قطعاً كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَاكَ إِلَّا كَافَّةً لِلنَّاسِ ) (۱) ﴿قُلْ إِنِّي رَسُولُ اللهِ إِليكم جَمِيعاً ) (۲) ﴿قُلْ أُوحِيَ إِليَّ أَنَّهُ اسْتَمَعَ نَفَرٌ مِنَ الجِنّ ...)(۳) الآيات ولكِنْ رَسُولَ اللهِ وخَاتَمَ النَّبِيِّينَ ) لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدين (٥) . لا يقال : ففي القرآن ما يدل على أن التوراة والإنجيل هدى للناس من غير تفرقة بين ما يوافق القرآن ويخالفه، فيختص هداية القرآن وبعثة محمد (عليه السلام) بقومه الذين هم العرب على ما يشير إليه بقوله : وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِنْ رَسُولٍ إِلَّا بِلِسَانِ قَوْمِهِ ) (٦) . لأنا نقول : هما هدى للناس من قبل نزول القرآن أو هدى لهم إلى الإيمان بمحمد (عليه السلام والاتباع لشريعته لما فيهما من البشارة ببعثته، والإنباء عن الاهتداء بمتابعته
He intends that he (the Prophet) is sent to the two weighty ones (humans and jinn), not to the Arabs specifically, as some Jews and Christians claim, claiming that the need for a prophet was only for the Arabs specifically, not for the People of the Two Books. This is refuted by what has passed of the need of all for one who renews the matter of the Sharia; rather, the need of the Jews and Christians is greater due to the corruption of their religion through alterations and types of misguidance, while they claim it is from Allah Almighty. The evidence for the universality of his mission and that he is the Seal of the Prophets, no prophet after him, and no abrogation of his Sharia, is that he claimed that in a way not susceptible to interpretation, and he manifested the miracle in accordance with it, and his miraculous book has testified to that decisively, such as His saying: 'And We have not sent you except as a universal [messenger] to mankind' (1), 'Say: Indeed I am the messenger of Allah to you all' (2), 'Say: It has been revealed to me that a group of jinn listened...' Commentary
This passage is an argument proving the universal mission of Prophet Muhammad (saw) and his seal of prophethood. The author first refutes the claim that a prophet was only needed for the Arabs, stating that all people, especially Jews and Christians, need a renewer of Sharia. Then he presents the evidence: the Prophet claimed universal prophethood clearly, supported by miracles and the Quran. He cites verses like 'We have not sent you except as a universal messenger to mankind' and 'Say: I am the messenger of Allah to you all' etc. Then he anticipates an objection: the Torah and Gospel are called guidance for all people, which might suggest that Muhammad's mission was only for Arabs. The author answers that those scriptures were guidance before the Quran or were guidance to believe in Muhammad and follow his Sharia, as they contained prophecies about him.

Jesus Follows Muhammad's Sharia
Answering the objection that Jesus's survival contradicts Muhammad's seal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the continued presence of Jesus (as) does not contradict Muhammad's status as the Seal of the Prophets.

Core Idea
Jesus will return as a follower of Muhammad, not a new prophet.

Some may wonder how Jesus (as) being alive and returning to earth can be reconciled with Muhammad being the final prophet. In this passage, the author addresses this objection directly, clarifying that Jesus will descend according to Muhammad's Sharia and will follow him, just as the Prophet said Moses would have done. This preserves the finality of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic and translation to see the objection about Jesus's continued existence and the author's answer.
Notice the author does not deny Jesus's life but reinterprets its meaning.
2
Identify the key principle
The author explains that Jesus will follow Muhammad's Sharia, meaning he will not bring a new law.
3
Connect to the Hadith
The author references a hadith where the Prophet said Moses would have followed him if alive. This strengthens the argument.
This analogy shows the continuity of prophethood under Muhammad.
4
Apply the concept
Reflect on how this preserves the meaning of 'Seal of the Prophets' — no new prophet with a new Sharia comes after Muhammad.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.

فإن قيل : أليس عيسى عليه السلام) حياً بعد نبينا، رفع إلى السماء، وسينزل إلى الدنيا؟ قلنا بلى ولكنه على شريعة نبينا، لا يسعه إلا اتباعه على ما قال (عليه السلام) في حق موسى أنه لو كان حياً لما وسعه إلا اتباعي، فيصح أنه خاتم الأنبياء، بمعنى أنه لا يبعث نبي بعده
If it is said: Is not Jesus (peace be upon him) alive after our Prophet, raised to heaven, and will descend to the earth? We say: Yes, but he is upon the Sharia of our Prophet; he cannot do other than follow him, as he (peace be upon him) said regarding Moses: 'If he were alive, he would have no choice but to follow me.' So it is correct that he (Muhammad) is the Seal of the Prophets, meaning that no prophet will be sent after him.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection regarding Jesus (as). The objector notes that Jesus is alive after our Prophet and will descend, which might seem to contradict Muhammad being the seal of prophets. The author answers that Jesus will descend but will follow Muhammad's Sharia, just as the Prophet said about Moses that if he were alive, he would follow him. Thus, Muhammad remains the seal in the sense that no new prophet with a new Sharia will come; Jesus will be a follower, not a new prophet.

Consensus and Evidences for Muhammad's Superiority
The author states the consensus and lists evidences for Muhammad's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the consensus that Muhammad is the best prophet and the key evidences for his superiority, including his community's excellence and his unique characteristics.

Core Idea
Muhammad's community's excellence proves his own excellence.

In this passage, the author presents the unanimous Muslim consensus that Prophet Muhammad is the best of all prophets. He then provides a range of evidences, from the excellence of his community as stated in the Quran to his unique roles and miracles. This lesson unpacks these proofs and also addresses the Prophet's humility in forbidding comparisons.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow from consensus to evidences.
Note the shift from positive claims to the humility hadith.
2
Identify the primary evidence
Focus on the argument that the excellence of the community implies the excellence of the messenger. Why is this logical?
The Quranic verses about the best community are key.
3
Explore the additional characteristics
List the unique qualities of Muhammad mentioned: sent to jinn and humans, seal of prophets, permanent miracle, abrogating Sharia, testimony over mankind.
These are distinct from the community argument.
4
Understand the humility hadith
The Prophet forbids preferring him over Moses and Jonah out of humility. How does this relate to his superiority?
The author clarifies it does not negate his rank.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأجمع المسلمون على أن أفضل الأنبياء محمد، لأن أمته خير الأمم لقوله تعالى: كُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ أُخْرِجَتْ لِلناسِ ) (۱) ﴿وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَاكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطَا (٢). وتفضيل الأمة من حيث إنها أمة تفضيل للرسول الذي هم أمته، ولأنه مبعوث إلى الثقلين، وخاتم الأنبياء والرسل ومعجزته الظاهرة الباهرة باقية على وجه الزمان، وشريعته ناسخة لجميع الأديان، وشهادته قائمة في القيامة على كافة البشر، الى غير ذلك من خصائص لا تعد ولا تحصى. وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَرَفعَ بعضهم دَرَجَاتِ ﴾ (۳) . إشارة إلى ذلك، والأحاديث الصحاح في هذا المعنى كثيرة، حتى قال (عليه السلام : أنا أكرم الأولين والآخرين على الله تعالى ولا فخر. كما قال (عليه السلام): لا تخيروني على موسى، وما ينبغي لعبد أن يقول : إني خير من يونس بن متى تواضع منه
And the Muslims have agreed that the best of the prophets is Muhammad, because his community is the best of communities, by His saying: 'You are the best community brought forth for mankind' (1) 'And thus We have made you a middle community' (2). And the preference of the community insofar as it is a community is a preference for the messenger whose community they are, and because he is sent to the two weighty ones, and the Seal of the Prophets and Messengers, and his manifest and dazzling miracle remains throughout time, and his Sharia abrogates all religions, and his testimony stands on the Day of Resurrection over all mankind, and other countless characteristics. And His saying: 'And We raised some of them above others in degrees' (3) is an indication of that, and the authentic hadiths on this meaning are many, until he (peace be upon him) said: 'I am the most honored of the first and the last with Allah Almighty, and I say this without pride.' And he also said: 'Do not give me superiority over Moses, and it is not befitting for a servant to say that I am better than Jonah son of Matta' — this out of humility.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents the consensus that Muhammad is the best of prophets. The evidence includes: his community is the best, as stated in the Quran ('You are the best community'), and the preference of the community implies the preference of the messenger. Additionally, his unique characteristics include being sent to both humans and jinn, being the seal, having a permanent miracle (the Quran), his Sharia abrogating all previous ones, and his testimony over mankind on Judgment Day. The author cites a verse about raising some in degrees and many hadiths, including the Prophet's statement that he is the most honored without pride, and his humbly forbidding people from preferring him over Moses or Jonah.

أمة وسطا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's statement forbidding preference over Moses and Jonah implies he is not superior to them.
Correction: The author clarifies that this was said out of humility (tawadu'), not as a denial of his actual rank.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that the Prophet, despite being the best of creation, spoke with such humility as to forbid preference over other prophets, what does that expose about the pride that often takes root in your own heart? In what specific situation this week will you consciously lower yourself as he did, not out of false modesty but out of genuine humility before Allah?
?
The Prophet's community is declared the best community. Do you live as a member of that community with the responsibility that comes with that status, or do you take comfort in the label while your actions betray indifference? What one habit must you change today to truly embody being from 'the best community'?
?
The Quran is the permanent miracle that abrogates all previous scriptures. Yet how often do you turn to it as your decisive guide, versus consulting it only when convenient? What would it look like for you to submit completely to the authority of this abrogating Sharia in a specific area of your life that you have been resisting?

Differing Views on the Best Prophet After Muhammad
Enumeration of opinions on the best prophet after Muhammad and Christian claim for Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the internal Islamic disagreements on the most excellent prophet after Muhammad and the Christian argument for Jesus' superiority.

Core Idea
Muslims agree Muhammad is best, but differ on the next; Christians claim Jesus surpasses all.

This passage from Sanusi's Sharh al-Maqasid surveys the various opinions within Islam on who is the best prophet after Muhammad, listing Adam, Noah, Abraham, Moses, and Jesus with supporting reasons. It then presents the Christian claim that Jesus is superior to all prophets, based on his miraculous birth, purity, and divine titles. Understanding these differing views clarifies the Islamic consensus on Muhammad's primacy and the boundaries of prophetic excellence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Notice the five opinions and the shift to the Christian argument.
2
Identify the five prophets and their reasons
List each prophet mentioned (Adam, Noah, Abraham, Moses, Jesus) and the specific virtue attributed to them in the text.
For example, Adam is 'father of mankind', Noah has 'long worship', etc.
3
Examine the Christian argument
The passage states that Christians give Jesus superiority because he is 'a word cast to Mary', 'a spirit from Him', pure, not created from sperm, etc. Notice the key phrases.
This argument contrasts with Islamic views.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider why this discussion matters: it affirms Muhammad's unique status while acknowledging diversity of opinion on secondary rank, and highlights Islamic refutation of Christian exceptionalism.
The author likely continues to refute the Christian claim in the original text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلفوا في الأفضل بعده، فقيل : آدم ، لكونه أبا البشر. وقيل: نوح لطول عبادته ومجاهدته . وقيل : إبراهيم لزيادة توكله واطمئنانه . وقيل : موسى، لكونه كليم الله ونجيه . وقيل : عيسى، لكونه روح الله وصفيه . وفضله النصارى على الكل بأنه كلمة ألقاها إلى مريم وروح منه ، طاهر مقدس ، لم يخلق من نطفة، وقد ولدته سيدة نساء العالمين المطهرة عن الأدناس، وتربى في حجر الأنبياء والأولياء، وتكلم
And they differed concerning who is the best after him (Muhammad). It was said: Adam, because he is the father of mankind. And it was said: Noah, due to the length of his worship and his struggle. And it was said: Abraham, due to his increased trust and tranquility. And it was said: Moses, because he is the interlocutor of Allah and His intimate. And it was said: Jesus, because he is the Spirit of Allah and His chosen one. And the Christians gave him superiority over all, (saying) that he is a word cast to Mary and a spirit from Him, pure and holy, not created from a sperm-drop, and the chief of the women of the worlds, purified from impurities, gave birth to him, and he was raised in the lap of the prophets and saints, and he spoke
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage enumerates the different scholarly opinions regarding the best prophet after Muhammad. Some say Adam due to being the father of humanity, others Noah for his long worship, Abraham for his trust, Moses for speaking with Allah, and Jesus for being the Spirit of Allah. Then the author mentions the Christian claim that Jesus is superior to all, based on his miraculous birth, purity, and upbringing. The passage ends mid-sentence ('and he spoke'), but it is clear that the author is presenting and likely refuting this Christian position, as the context of the book is kalam defending Islamic beliefs.

Checkpoint
Which prophet is said to be the best after Muhammad according to those who prioritize being the 'interlocutor of Allah'?
A) Adam
B) Noah
C) Abraham
D) Moses

Key Takeaway
The passage shows that Islamic scholarly tradition acknowledges different views on the secondary rank of prophets, but the Christian claim for Jesus' superiority is presented as a contrast to Islamic consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that scholars differed on who is the best prophet after Muhammad, does it challenge your assumption that everything in Islam is unanimously agreed upon? How does this variety strengthen or weaken your trust in Islamic scholarship?
?
The Christians claim Jesus is superior to all prophets based on his miraculous birth and purity. How does your own belief in Muhammad ﷺ as the best prophet affect the way you view Jesus? Do you respect him less or more, and why?
?
Of the prophets listed (Adam, Noah, Abraham, Moses, Jesus), which one do you feel the closest personal connection to, and what does that say about the virtue you need most in your own life right now?
